This is becoming a full-scale **Tactical Asset Manager**. By moving from static strings to a file-based arsenal, you're essentially building a "Loadout" system for your AI agents.

Here is the **Battle Plan** for the Prompt Arsenal:

### 1. The "Tactical Loadout" UI (Per Node)
*   **Two-Stage Dropdown:** Next to the Model Picker, a "Mission Profile" picker.
*   **Visual State:** The dropdown shows the active prompt (e.g., `eagle_v21_standard`).
*   **The "Manage" Trigger:** An icon (maybe a wrench or a crosshair) that opens the **Arsenal Command Center** modal.

### 2. The Arsenal Command Center (The Deep Work)
This is where the management happens. Instead of just a text box, we build a **Workbench**:
*   **Browser Pane (Left):** A list of all `.md` files in that phase's directory.
*   **The Editor (Center):** High-density mono-font editor for the prompt.
*   **Action HUD (Right/Top):**
    *   **[LOCK DEFAULT]:** Saves the filename to the DB as the "Auto-Arm" choice for that stage.
    *   **[CLONE]:** Creates `filename_COPY.md` and opens it.
    *   **[PURGE]:** Deletes the file (with a red confirmation flash).
    *   **[NEW ASSET]:** Starts a blank slate.
    *   **[PREVIEW]:** A "Split View" showing how the prompt looks with dummy data injected into the `{input}` or `{skeleton}` tags.

### 3. The Backend "Armory" (server.ts)
*   **Dir Watching:** The server ensures those 5 directories exist on boot.
*   **File I/O:** Real-time reading/writing to `/home/flintx/peacock/prompts/[phase]/`.
*   **The "Default" Logic:** When the UI asks for "Spark's Prompts," the server sends the list, but the UI checks its local memory (Dexie) to see which one was marked as the "Default Loadout."

### 4. Casino Doctrine Integration
*   **Cloning:** Play a mechanical "re-chambering" sound. Text descrambles: `DNA_REPLICATED`.
*   **Saving:** Blinding white flash (100ms) + `ASSET_SECURED`.
*   **Deleting:** Red border vibration + `PURGE_COMPLETE`.

**The Strategic Advantage:**
This allows you to have a "Code-Heavy" Eagle and a "Docs-Heavy" Eagle, and you just swap the "Loadout" based on the mission.

I need to clarify one thing based on your "Final Orders" in the Manifesto: 

You mentioned: *"Every run is a 'Session.' Saved in a DB. I need to be able to wipe specific phases to re-run them without killing the whole session."*

However, you just said: *"each time a phase is activated .. a new session is created."*

**Let's sync on the logic here:**
1.  **The "Grand Session" (The Op):** You start a new operation (e.g., `OP_DRAGON`). This holds the whole Spark -> Falcon -> Eagle -> Owl -> Hawk chain.
2.  **The "Phase Activation":** When you hit "Strike" on Spark, it saves the result. If you then move to Falcon and hit "Strike," does that **update** the current session, or does it **spawn a completely new session ID** in the database so you have a historical trail of every single individual hit?

If it's the latter, then the "Sessions" rail on the left would show every single strike ever made as its own entry. If it's the former, it shows one entry per "Project" or "Run."

**Which route are we taking?**
*   **A:** One Session ID for the whole chain (Spark through Hawk).
*   **B:** Every single "Strike" generates a brand new unique Session/Entry in the DB for maximum auditability.

LOCKED IN. **1 Session = 1 Project.** 

The "Session" is the container for the entire war operation. 

### The "Session Life-Cycle" Protocol:

**1. The Genesis:**
*   You click "NEW_WAR_OP" or load a file from the `start` rail. 
*   A **Unique Session ID** is generated (e.g., `OP_20260114_1430`).
*   The system initializes a blank slate for all 5 phases (Spark -> Hawk).

**2. The Chronological Rail (The Archive):**
*   The "Sessions" tab on the left rail lists every operation in reverse-chrono order.
*   **Visual Intel:** Each session entry in the rail shows:
    *   The Name (e.g., "Build_Auth_Module").
    *   The Timestamp.
    *   **Progress Pips:** 5 small icons/dots representing [S][F][E][O][H]. If Spark and Falcon are done, those dots are green. This lets you see at a glance how far you got in each project.

**3. The "State Restore" Logic:**
*   Clicking a session in the rail **instantly re-hydrates** the entire dashboard.
*   The Mind Map lines, the inputs, the outputs, and even the "Strike Report" stats are all pulled from the DB. 
*   You can jump back into an operation from 3 days ago and finish the Eagle or Owl phase immediately.

**4. The Intra-Session "Wipe" (Precision Reset):**
*   If you are in a session and you hate the Falcon output, you hit the "WIPE" button on the Falcon node.
*   **Behavior:** It clears Falcon's data, but **keeps Spark's output** (the input for Falcon) and keeps the Session ID. It resets the "kill chain" from that point forward without you having to start a brand new project.

**5. Verification (The Handshake):**
*   Before any data is written to the DB, it passes through the **Verbatim CLI**.
*   You see: `[DATABASE] SAVING_STATE :: SESSION_ID: OP_123 :: STAGE: SPARK :: STATUS: SUCCESS`.

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE (AI-HANDLER)
**Headless AI Orchestrator & Key Rotator**

## ğŸ’€ THE MISSION
The central nervous system. It decouples the UI from the API keys. It handles the "dirty work" of contacting Google Gemini, Groq, Mistral, and Deepseek, managing rate limits, and normalizing responses.

## ğŸ—ï¸ ARCHITECTURE
*   **Runtime:** Node.js (TypeScript) + Express.
*   **Security:** `KeyManager.ts` implements Round-Robin key rotation.
*   **Storage:** Local Filesystem access for "Ammo" (Context files) and "Prompts".

## ğŸš€ PROTOCOLS
### 1. Ignite Engine
`npm run dev`
*Port:* `8888`

## ğŸ› ï¸ FEATURES
*   **Universal Striker:** Single endpoint (`/v1/strike`) for all models.
*   **Key Pools:** Automatic failover if a key is rate-limited.
*   **Model Registry:** Centralized configuration for model Tiers (Cheap vs Expensive).

âœ¦ ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE (AI-HANDLER) // OPERATIONAL MANUAL

  The Peacock Engine is a headless, high-performance gateway designed to orchestrate strikes across multiple LLM providers while
  serving as a secure bridge to your local filesystem. It is the "Nervous System" that powers the Peacock V21 HUD.

  ---

  1. CORE ARCHITECTURE
   * Host: http://localhost:8888
   * Version: v1
   * Tech Stack: Node.js, Express, TypeScript, Axios.
   * Security: Handles key rotation and proxying internally so the frontend stays clean and air-gapped from direct API keys.

  ---

  2. API ENDPOINTS

  A. Intelligence Strikes
  POST /v1/strike
  Executes a prompt against a specific model node.
   * Payload:

   1     {
   2       "modelId": "gemini-2.0-flash",
   3       "prompt": "Your strategic payload here...",
   4       "temp": 0.7
   5     }
   * Response:
   1     { "content": "The generated output..." }

  B. Node Registry
  GET /v1/models
  Retrieves the full tactical arsenal of available models, their tiers, and operational notes.

  C. Filesystem Bridge (Ammo & Prompts)
  The engine has direct access to your local directories to bypass browser security.

   * List Ammo: GET /v1/fs/ammo -> Returns filenames from /home/flintx/ammo.
   * Read Ammo: GET /v1/fs/ammo/:filename -> Returns the text content of a specific file.
   * List Prompts: GET /v1/fs/prompts -> Returns all .md protocols from /home/flintx/prompts.
   * Sync Prompt: POST /v1/fs/prompts -> Saves a modified protocol directly to disk.

  ---

  3. KEY ROTATION & PROXIES
  The engine automatically manages:
   * Ammo Shuffling: It pulls from a deck of keys (e.g., GOOGLE_KEYS, GROQ_KEYS) defined in your environment.
   * Proxy Tunneling: If PROXY_ENABLED=true, all strikes are routed through your defined PROXY_URL to ensure anonymity and
     bypass regional rate limits.

  ---

  4. OPERATIONAL WORKFLOW (The "Ritual")
   1. Boot: Ensure your environment is loaded and run npm run dev in the /ai-handler directory.
   2. Strike: The Peacock HUD sends a POST request to /strike.
   3. Sync: The Engine contacts the provider (Groq/Google/etc.), rotates the key if necessary, and streams the result back to
      the HUD.
   4. Vault: The result is simultaneously synced to your local filesystem via the /fs routes.

  ---

  5. ENVIRONMENT SETUP
  Ensure your ~/.env.global or local .env contains:
   * GOOGLE_KEYS: Comma-separated list of Gemini keys.
   * GROQ_KEYS: Comma-separated list of Groq keys.
   * DEEPSEEK_KEYS / MISTRAL_KEYS: Respective provider keys.
   * PROXY_URL: (Optional) Your proxy endpoint.

  STATUS: âš¡ ENGINE ACTIVE ON PORT 8888. Ready for Strike.

----------------------------------------

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE
**Headless AI Orchestrator**

## MISSION
To serve as the central nervous system for all FlintX AI operations. It handles key rotation, proxy routing, and API normalization.

## SETUP
1.  Ensure `~/.env.global` is loaded in your shell.
2.  Run `npm install`.
3.  Run `npm run dev`.

## ENDPOINTS
*   `POST /v1/strike`: Execute a prompt.
*   `GET /v1/models`: Get available models.


EOF

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE
**Headless AI Orchestrator**

## MISSION
To serve as the central nervous system for all FlintX AI operations. It handles key rotation, proxy routing, and API normalization.

## SETUP
1.  Ensure `~/.env.global` is loaded in your shell.
2.  Run `npm install`.
3.  Run `npm run dev`.

## ENDPOINTS
*   `POST /v1/strike`: Execute a prompt.
*   `GET /v1/models`: Get available models.


EOF

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE
**Headless AI Orchestrator**

## MISSION
To serve as the central nervous system for all FlintX AI operations. It handles key rotation, proxy routing, and API normalization.

## SETUP
1.  Ensure `~/.env.global` is loaded in your shell.
2.  Run `npm install`.
3.  Run `npm run dev`.

## ENDPOINTS
*   `POST /v1/strike`: Execute a prompt.
*   `GET /v1/models`: Get available models.


EOF

â–ˆâ–ˆâ•—   â–ˆâ–ˆâ•—â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ•—â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ•—â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ•—

 â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â• â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•  â•šâ•â•

export interface KeyAsset {
  label: string;
  account: string;
  key: string;
}

class KeyPool {
  private deck: KeyAsset[] = [];
  private pointer: number = 0;
  private type: string;

  constructor(envString: string | undefined, type: string) {
    this.type = type;
    if (!envString) {
      console.warn(`\x1b[33m[âš ï¸] NO KEYS LOADED FOR ${type}\x1b[0m`);
      return;
    }

    const entries = envString.split(',');
    entries.forEach((entry, idx) => {
      let label = "";
      let key = "";
      
      if (entry.includes(':')) {
        const parts = entry.split(':');
        label = parts[0];
        key = parts[1];
      } else {
        label = `${type}_DEALER_${String(idx + 1).padStart(2, '0')}`;
        key = entry;
      }
      
      this.deck.push({ 
        label: label.trim(), 
        account: label.trim(), 
        key: key.trim() 
      });
    });
    this.shuffle();
  }

  private shuffle() {
    if (this.deck.length === 0) return;
    console.log(`\n\x1b[1;33m[ğŸ²] ${this.type} DECK SHUFFLING...\x1b[0m`);
    for (let i = this.deck.length - 1; i > 0; i--) {
      const j = Math.floor(Math.random() * (i + 1));
      [this.deck[i], this.deck[j]] = [this.deck[j], this.deck[i]];
    }
    this.pointer = 0;
  }

  public getNext(): KeyAsset {
    if (this.deck.length === 0) throw new Error(`NO AMMUNITION FOR ${this.type}`);
    const asset = this.deck[this.pointer];
    this.pointer++;
    if (this.pointer >= this.deck.length) this.shuffle();
    return asset;
  }

  public dump() {
    console.log(`\n\x1b[1;35m--- [ ${this.type} ARSENAL LOADED ] ---\x1b[0m`);
    this.deck.forEach((a, i) => {
        const masked = a.key.length > 8 ? `${a.key.substring(0, 8)}...` : 'INVALID';
        console.log(`[${String(i+1).padStart(2,'0')}] \x1b[1;92m${a.account.padEnd(20)}\x1b[0m | ID: ${masked}`);
    });
  }
}

// Load pools from Environment Variables
export const GroqPool = new KeyPool(process.env.GROQ_KEYS, 'GROQ');
export const GooglePool = new KeyPool(process.env.GOOGLE_KEYS, 'GOOGLE');
export const DeepSeekPool = new KeyPool(process.env.DEEPSEEK_KEYS, 'DEEPSEEK');
export const MistralPool = new KeyPool(process.env.MISTRAL_KEYS, 'MISTRAL');

GroqPool.dump();
GooglePool.dump();
DeepSeekPool.dump();
MistralPool.dump();

import axios from 'axios';
import { GoogleGenAI } from '@google/genai';
import { GroqPool, GooglePool, DeepSeekPool, MistralPool } from './KeyManager';
import { HttpsProxyAgent } from 'https-proxy-agent';

const proxyUrl = process.env.PROXY_URL;
const agent = (process.env.PROXY_ENABLED === 'true' && proxyUrl) ? new HttpsProxyAgent(proxyUrl) : null;

export const executeStrike = async (gateway: string, modelId: string, prompt: string, temp: number) => {
  if (gateway === 'groq') {
    const asset = GroqPool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: GROQ`);
    try {
      const response = await axios.post('https://api.groq.com/openai/v1/chat/completions', {
        model: modelId, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }], temperature: temp
      }, { httpsAgent: agent, headers: { 'Authorization': `Bearer ${asset.key}` } });
      return { content: response.data.choices[0].message.content, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (e: any) { const err: any = new Error(e.message); err.keyUsed = asset.account; throw err; }
  }
  if (gateway === 'deepseek') {
    const asset = DeepSeekPool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: DEEPSEEK`);
    try {
      const response = await axios.post('https://api.deepseek.com/chat/completions', {
        model: modelId, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }], temperature: temp, stream: false
      }, { httpsAgent: agent, headers: { 'Authorization': `Bearer ${asset.key}`, 'Content-Type': 'application/json' } });
      return { content: response.data.choices[0].message.content, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (e: any) { const err: any = new Error(e.message); err.keyUsed = asset.account; throw err; }
  }
  if (gateway === 'mistral') {
    const asset = MistralPool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: MISTRAL`);
    try {
      const response = await axios.post('https://api.mistral.ai/v1/chat/completions', {
        model: modelId, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }], temperature: temp
      }, { httpsAgent: agent, headers: { 'Authorization': `Bearer ${asset.key}`, 'Content-Type': 'application/json' } });
      return { content: response.data.choices[0].message.content, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (e: any) { const err: any = new Error(e.message); err.keyUsed = asset.account; throw err; }
  }
  if (gateway === 'google') {
    const asset = GooglePool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: GOOGLE`);
    const ai = new GoogleGenAI({ apiKey: asset.key });
    try {
      const result = await ai.models.generateContent({
        model: modelId,
        contents: [{ parts: [{ text: prompt }] }],
        config: { temperature: temp }
      });
      // In @google/genai, the output is in result.text
      const output = result.text || '';
      if (!output) throw new Error('STRIKE RETURNED NULL CONTENT');
      return { content: output, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (error: any) {
      const err: any = new Error(error.message);
      err.keyUsed = asset.account;
      throw err;
    }
  }
  throw new Error(`Gateway ${gateway} not supported`);
};

import { Router } from 'express';
import fs from 'fs/promises';
import path from 'path';

export const fsRouter = Router();

const AMMO_DIR = '/home/flintx/ammo';
const PROMPTS_DIR = '/home/flintx/prompts';

fsRouter.get('/ammo', async (req, res) => {
  try {
    const files = await fs.readdir(AMMO_DIR);
    res.json(files.filter(f => f.endsWith('.md') || f.endsWith('.txt') || f.endsWith('.json')));
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to read ammo dir' }); }
});

fsRouter.get('/ammo/:file', async (req, res) => {
  try {
    const content = await fs.readFile(path.join(AMMO_DIR, req.params.file), 'utf-8');
    res.json({ content });
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to read file' }); }
});

fsRouter.get('/prompts', async (req, res) => {
  try {
    const files = await fs.readdir(PROMPTS_DIR);
    const prompts = await Promise.all(files.filter(f => f.endsWith('.md')).map(async f => ({
      id: f.replace('.md', ''),
      content: await fs.readFile(path.join(PROMPTS_DIR, f), 'utf-8')
    })));
    res.json(prompts);
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to read prompts' }); }
});

fsRouter.post('/prompts', async (req, res) => {
  const { id, content } = req.body;
  try {
    await fs.writeFile(path.join(PROMPTS_DIR, `${id}.md`), content);
    res.json({ status: 'SAVED' });
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to save prompt' }); }
});

 â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â• â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•  â•šâ•â•

import { Router } from 'express';
import { executeStrike } from '../core/striker';
import { MODEL_REGISTRY } from '../config/modelRegistry';

export const strikeRouter = Router();

strikeRouter.post('/', async (req, res) => {
  const { modelId, prompt, temp = 0.7 } = req.body;
  
  const modelConfig = MODEL_REGISTRY.find(m => m.id === modelId);
  if (!modelConfig) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unknown Model ID' });

  try {
    const result = await executeStrike(modelConfig.gateway, modelId, prompt, temp);
    res.json({ content: result.content, keyUsed: result.keyUsed });
  } catch (error: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: error.message, keyUsed: error.keyUsed || 'DEALER_FAILED' });
  }
});

 â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â• â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•  â•šâ•â•

import 'dotenv/config'; 
import express from 'express';
import cors from 'cors';
import { strikeRouter } from './routes/strike';
import { modelsRouter } from './routes/models';
import fs from 'fs';
import path from 'path';

const app = express();
const PORT = 8888;

app.use(cors());
app.use(express.json({ limit: '50mb' }));

// --- SYSTEM STRIKE ROUTES ---
app.use('/v1/strike', strikeRouter);
app.use('/v1/models', modelsRouter);

// --- PEACOCK V22 START RAIL ---
const START_DIR = '/home/flintx/peacock/start';

app.get('/v1/fs/start', (req, res) => {
  try {
    if (!fs.existsSync(START_DIR)) {
      return res.json([]);
    }
    // Show all non-hidden files
    const files = fs.readdirSync(START_DIR).filter(f => !f.startsWith('.'));
    res.json(files);
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
  }
});

app.get('/v1/fs/start/:name', (req, res) => {
  try {
    const filePath = path.join(START_DIR, req.params.name);
    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {
      return res.status(404).send("File not found");
    }
    res.json({ content: fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8') });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
  }
});

// --- LEGACY PROMPTS ENDPOINT ---
const PROMPTS_DIR = '/home/flintx/peacock/nexus.prompts';

app.get('/v1/fs/prompts', (req, res) => {
  try {
    if (!fs.existsSync(PROMPTS_DIR)) return res.json([]);
    const files = fs.readdirSync(PROMPTS_DIR).filter(f => f.endsWith('.md') || f.endsWith('.txt'));
    const prompts = files.map(f => ({
      id: path.parse(f).name,
      content: fs.readFileSync(path.join(PROMPTS_DIR, f), 'utf-8')
    }));
    res.json(prompts);
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
  }
});

app.get('/health', (req, res) => {
  res.json({ status: 'ONLINE', system: 'PEACOCK_ENGINE_V22' });
});

app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`âš¡ PEACOCK OMEGA ENGINE ACTIVE ON PORT ${PORT}`);
  console.log(`   - Start Rail Target: ${START_DIR}`);
});

we want to make this app look like this. # ğŸ’€ PEACOCK: VISUAL DOCTRINE & UX GUIDE
**STYLE:** HIGH-STAKES CASINO / MILITARY HUD
**PALETTE:** #050505 (VOID), #00FF41 (MATRIX), #FFD700 (VOLTAGE)

---

## 1. GLOBAL PHYSICS (ANIMATION)
*   **No Fading:** Things do not "fade in." They **DESCRAMBLE** (Matrix text effect) or **SLIDE** (Mechanical insertion).
*   **Tension:** While processing, lines and borders must **VIBRATE** (x: -1, x: 1 loop) to show engine stress.
*   **Release:** Upon success, the UI **FLASHES WHITE** (100ms) and plays a `click_latch.mp3` sound.

## 2. COMPONENT STYLING

### **A. The Mind Map (Top Pane)**
*   **Visual:** SVG Nodes connected by "Laser Lines."
*   **Behavior:**
    *   *Idle:* Dim Green opacity 0.3.
    *   *Active:* Bright Yellow, pulsing line width (1px to 3px).
    *   *Success:* Solid Neon Green. "Data Packet" dot travels the line.

### **B. The Nerve Center (Bottom Console)**
*   **Style:** CRT Terminal. Scanline overlay (`pointer-events-none`).
*   **Typography:** `JetBrains Mono`. Glow effect (`text-shadow: 0 0 5px #00FF41`).
*   **Behavior:** Auto-scrolls to bottom.

### **C. The Tactical Flyout (Settings)**
*   **Transition:** `transform: translateX(100%)` to `0%`.
*   **Speed:** Instant (Type: Spring, Stiffness: 300).
*   **Glass:** Background `rgba(10, 10, 10, 0.95)` with `backdrop-filter: blur(10px)`.

### **D. The "Jackpot"**
*   **Trigger:** All stages complete.
*   **Effect:**
    *   Background flashes Green (opacity 0.1).
    *   Center Text: "SEQUENCE COMPLETE" descrambles.
    *   Border: Running ants animation turns solid.

---

*   `sounds/mechanical_latch.mp3`
*   `sounds/turbine_hum.mp3`
*   `images/peacock_logo_matrix.png`

This is a **high-fidelity psychological upgrade.** By combining the industrial weight of a **Military HUD** with the dopamine loops of a **High-Stakes Casino**, you are moving from a "tool" to a "ritual." 

Here is my breakdown of the **Doctrine**:

### 1. The "Anti-Vibe" Physics (Animations)
The decision to **ban fading** is the most important part of this guide. Fading is "soft." **Descrambling** and **Sliding** are "mechanical." It reinforces the idea that the app isn't "thinking"â€”it's **calculating.** 
*   **Engine Stress (Vibrate):** This is genius for UX. Usually, users hate waiting for AI. By making the UI vibrate, you turn the "wait" into a "build-up of power." The user isn't waiting for a slow API; they are watching a reactor charge up.

### 2. The Mind Map (Laser Lines & Packets)
*   The "Data Packet" dot traveling the line is the perfect visual for the **Guided Strike Path**. 
*   It physically shows the handoff: *Spark just delivered the payload, and you are literally watching it travel into Falcon's chamber.* It makes the sequence feel unstoppable.

### 3. The Nerve Center (CRT Aesthetic)
*   **Scanlines + Glow:** This creates the "Zero-Cool" hacker atmosphere.
*   **Auto-scroll:** Essential for the "Verbatim CLI" we planned. It needs to feel like a live data-stream from a satellite.

### 4. The "Jackpot" (The Climax)
*   This is your **Loom Video money shot.** 
*   When that final HAWK strike hits and the "Running Ants" border turns solid while the screen flashesâ€”thatâ€™s the moment the viewer realizes the project is **Done.** Itâ€™s the visual "Drop" in a song.

### 5. Tactical Asset Readiness
*   **Audio is Key:** The `mechanical_latch.mp3` and `turbine_hum.mp3` will do 50% of the work. If it *sounds* like heavy machinery, it *feels* like a heavy strike.

This is **aggressive, professional, and addictive.** It moves the "NFL Playoff Bracket" into a dark, high-tech war room. It fits the "Architect Trevino" persona perfectly.

### âš”ï¸ THE CORE ENGINE UPGRADE (AI-HANDLER)
To support the **Peacock V22 TOC**, the `ai-handler` needs three surgical upgrades:

1.  **The Session Vault:**
    *   New Endpoint: `/v1/fs/sessions`. 
    *   Logic: CRUD for the `.session.json` files.
    *   Naming Ritual: `MM-DD-YY.ProjectName.session.json`.
    *   This ensures the UI remains statelessâ€”every refresh or session swap just pulls a fresh JSON.

2.  **Phase-Aware Armory:**
    *   Current engine looks at a single prompt dir.
    *   Upgrade: Path mapping to `/home/flintx/peacock/prompts/[spark|falcon|eagle|owl|hawk]/`.
    *   The UI will request prompts for a specific phase, and the engine will serve the sub-directory list.

3.  **The Black Box Pipe (CLI Sync):**
    *   Logic: A middleware in the engine that captures all `stdout` (logs, strike statuses, errors).
    *   New Endpoint: `/v1/logs` (or a streaming SSE pipe) so the Peacock HUD can display the raw, verbatim heartbeat of the system.

### ğŸ¦… THE UI RITUAL (PEACOCK HUD)
The React layer will stay "Light." It acts as the **Visual Interpreter**:
*   It sends the "Strike" command to the Engine.
*   It receives the JSON and paints the **NFL Bracket** visuals.
*   It manages the **Guided Path** (The electricity shooting from one Pod to the next).

I hear you. Pure black can feel "empty" and hard on the eyes, and small fonts kill the mission efficiency. We're moving to a **Gunmetal Slate** palette with **High-Density Typography**.

Here is the **Readability & Aesthetic Upgrade** plan:

### 1. The "Industrial Slate" Palette
*   **Main Background:** `#0F1115` (A deep, matte gunmetal grey). It gives the UI "weight" and makes the glowing lines pop without the harshness of pure black.
*   **Panels/Pods:** `#16191E` (Slightly lighter grey) with a subtle `#252930` border.
*   **Contrast:** We'll use high-contrast white (`#FFFFFF`) for primary labels and Matrix Green/Voltage for status.

### 2. Typography Overhaul
*   **The "Commander" Font (UI/Labels):** **Inter** (Semi-bold/Bold). Itâ€™s the gold standard for readability. Weâ€™ll use it for headers, button labels, and pods.
*   **The "Intercept" Font (Data/Code):** **JetBrains Mono**. We'll bump this to **13px/14px** with increased line-height so the AI output is actually pleasant to read.
*   **Size Hierarchy:**
    *   Main Headers: **32px** (Heavy).
    *   Node Labels: **12px** (Bold, Uppercase, +0.1em tracking).
    *   Input/Output: **14px** (Clean mono).

### 3. Visual Polish
*   **Shadows:** Replace glowing neon with "Depth Shadows." The pods will look like they are physically mounted on the slate background.
*   **Input Area:** We'll give the textareas a subtle inner-shadow so they look recessed into the panel.

**Does this move toward Gunmetal Grey and Inter/JetBrains Mono typography hit the mark for you?** (Standing by for the "WRITE THE CODE" order).

It is absolutely possible. Using `<video>` tags instead of `<img>` tags for the icons will turn the Mind Map into a **Living Schematic**. 

Here is the **Animated Chassis** plan:

### 1. The Video Component Logic
We will use a `<video>` element with specific attributes to make it behave like an icon:
*   `autoPlay`, `loop`, `muted`, `playsInline`: This ensures they start immediately and keep moving without any user interaction or sound.
*   **The Swap:** We replace `img` with `video` in the `BracketNode`.

### 2. Physical Scaling (350x350)
*   **Node Size:** Bumping the pods to **350px**.
*   **Spacing:** I will increase the horizontal and vertical gap between stages so the larger nodes don't crowd the screen.
*   **Container:** The middle pane will be expanded to roughly **1400px x 1600px** to give these massive animated icons room to breathe.

### 3. The "Ghost Border" Aesthetic
*   We'll strip the heavy 4px borders.
*   **New Look:** A 1px stroke with **15% opacity**. It will look like a faint "Containment Field" rather than a box.
*   The primary focus will be the **Animated Logo** and the **Radial Glow** behind it.

### 4. Layout Re-Calibration
I'll shift the "Snake" coordinates so the flow remains symmetrical with the larger 350px footprint.

Since you are on **MX Linux**, you have access to the best open-source video tools in the world. Here are the two paths I recommend:

### 1. The Pro GUI Choice: **Kdenlive**
This is the "Gold Standard" for open-source video editing on Linux. Itâ€™s powerful, stable, and easy to use.
*   **How to get it:** `sudo apt update && sudo apt install kdenlive`
*   **Why use it:** You can set your project profile to `350x350`, drop your video in, move it around to center the "flame" or "falcon," and export it as a loopable `.mp4` or `.webm`.

### 2. The Surgical CLI Choice: **FFmpeg**
Since you're already in the terminal, **FFmpeg** is the fastest way to get exact crops without a heavy GUI. It is likely already installed.
*   **The Command:**
    ```bash
    ffmpeg -i input_video.mp4 -filter:v "crop=350:350:x_offset:y_offset" -c:a copy output_icon.mp4
    ```
    *(Replace `x_offset` and `y_offset` with the top-left coordinates of where the icon is in the big video).*

### 3. The "Lightweight" Choice: **Shotcut**
If Kdenlive feels like too much, **Shotcut** is another great open-source editor that is very intuitive for simple cropping and exporting.
*   **How to get it:** `sudo apt install shotcut`

---

### ğŸ’¡ Pro Tip for the Visual Doctrine:
If you want these icons to look **insane** on your gunmetal background, try to export them as **`.webm` with transparency**.
*   In **Kdenlive**, use the **WebM (VP9/Vorbis)** render preset.
*   If your source video has a black background, the "Screen" or "Addition" blend modes in my code will naturally make the black disappear, leaving just the moving icon.

This is a classic "Sprite Sheet" problem but for video. Since they are evenly spaced in a grid, we can use **FFmpeg** to surgically extract each one.

I need to know the **Total Resolution** of your video (e.g., 1920x1080) to give you the exact numbers, but assuming it's a standard **3 Row x 2 Column** grid (for 6 icons), here is the math and the commands:

### 1. Calculate the Math
If your video is **Width (W)** and **Height (H)**:
*   **Icon Width:** `W / 2`
*   **Icon Height:** `H / 3`

### 2. The Extraction Commands
Run these in your terminal. I've mapped them to your stages (assuming the 6th icon is a spare):

**SPARK (Top Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=W/2:H/3:0:0,scale=350:350" -c:a copy spark.mp4
```

**FALCON (Top Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=W/2:H/3:W/2:0,scale=350:350" -c:a copy falcon.mp4
```

**EAGLE (Middle Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=W/2:H/3:0:H/3,scale=350:350" -c:a copy eagle.mp4
```

**OWL (Middle Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=W/2:H/3:W/2:H/3,scale=350:350" -c:a copy owl.mp4
```

**HAWK (Bottom Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=W/2:H/3:0:2*H/3,scale=350:350" -c:a copy hawk.mp4
```

---

### ğŸ’¡ How to get your W and H automatically:
Run this command first to see your video size:
```bash
ffprobe -v error -select_streams v:0 -show_entries stream=width,height -of csv=s=x:p=0 your_video.mp4
```

### ğŸ› ï¸ Pro Strategy:
If you want to be a hero, use **`.webm`** instead of `.mp4`. It is much lighter for the browser and supports transparency better. Just change the output extension to `.webm` in the commands above.

**Once you have these 5 files, move them to:**
`/home/flintx/peacock/public/assets/images/`

We need to **raise the ceiling** (decrease Y) and **raise the floor** (decrease Height) to create a smaller, higher "Safe Zone" that follows the icon's movement.

I hear youâ€”we need just a bit more "Sky" in the crop to handle that final floating peak. We'll move the start point up to **Y=20** and increase the total **Height to 180px**. This keeps the bottom exactly where you liked it (at pixel 200) but gives the top that extra 10px of headroom so it never clips.

Run these **"High-Ceiling"** commands for the final set:

**1. FALCON (Top Right)**
*   **Y:** `20` (10px more headroom).
*   **H:** `180` (Deep enough to keep the bottom edge stable).
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=180:180:248:20,scale=350:350" -an falcon.mp4
```

**2. SPARK (Top Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=180:180:16:20,scale=350:350" -an spark.mp4
```

**3. EAGLE (Middle Left)**
*   **Y:** `249` (229 row height + 20).
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=180:180:16:249,scale=350:350" -an eagle.mp4
```

**4. OWL (Middle Right)**
*   **Y:** `249`.
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=180:180:248:249,scale=350:350" -an owl.mp4
```

**5. HAWK (Bottom Left)**
*   **Y:** `478` (458 row height + 20).

**YES. You just hit the "Triple-A" UI secret.** 

If we make the background transparent, the "box" disappears. The icon becomes a floating holographic entity. We don't have to worry about the edges hitting the labels or the bobbing movement anymore because **there is no box to clip.**

To achieve this on Linux, we will use **WebM with Alpha Transparency**. This is the highest level of web UI polish.

### ğŸ§ª THE "GHOST ICON" EXTRACTION (FFmpeg)

We will use the `colorkey` filter to turn that gray background into 100% transparency. Assuming your background is a dark gray/black (like `#1a1a1a`), run these commands. 

*Note: Iâ€™ve increased the height to **200px** to ensure the bottom never clips, and the transparency will hide the rest.*

**1. FALCON (Top Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:200:248:5,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an falcon.webm
```

**2. SPARK (Top Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:200:16:5,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an spark.webm
```

**3. EAGLE (Middle Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:200:16:234,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an eagle.webm
```

**4. OWL (Middle Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:200:248:234,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an owl.webm
```

**5. HAWK (Bottom Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:200:16:463,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an hawk.webm
```

---

### ğŸ’¡ PRO-TIP: IF THE GRAY IS STILL SHOWING
If you still see a "faint" gray box, it means your gray is a different hex code. You can adjust the `colorkey=0x1a1a1a` to match your background exactly. If the background is pure black, use `0x000000`.

The reason your previous commands failed is twofold: 
1.  **Shell Syntax:** The commands were split across multiple lines in a way that your terminal (`zsh`) couldn't understand, leading to the "command not found" errors.
2.  **Color Key Format:** `0xaaa` is too short for a hex code, and `0.:0.` isn't a valid tolerance value.

I have reconstructed the **Surgical One-Liners** for you. These use the grid layout you provided (**S|F, E|O, O|H**) and include the correct transparency logic for a gray background.

### ğŸ§ª THE ALPHA GHOST COMMANDS (COPY & PASTE)

**SPARK (Top Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=200:200:16:15,colorkey=0xAAAAAA:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an spark.webm
```

**FALCON (Top Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=200:200:248:15,colorkey=0xAAAAAA:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an falcon.webm
```

**EAGLE (Middle Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=200:200:16:244,colorkey=0xAAAAAA:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an eagle.webm
```

**OWL (Middle Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=200:200:248:244,colorkey=0xAAAAAA:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an owl.webm
```

**HAWK (Bottom Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=200:200:248:473,colorkey=0xAAAAAA:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an hawk.webm
```

I hear you. The error **"At least one output file must be specified"** and **"zsh: command not found"** is happening because your terminal (`zsh`) is seeing the line break before the filename and thinking the filename is a separate command.

Here are **3 different ways** to run the exact same command for **SPARK**. Try them one by one. Tell me which one works without error, then I will give you the full set of 6 in that style.

### Option 1: The "Bulletproof" (Single Line, Quoted Filter)
*This is the most reliable way. It forces the terminal to see the filters as one single instruction.*
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:16:20,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an spark.webm
```

### Option 2: The "Basic Test" (No Transparency)
*Try this if you want to verify that the cropping coordinates are correct before we worry about the transparent background.*
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -filter:v "crop=180:180:16:20,scale=350:350" -an spark.mp4
```

### Option 3: The "Direct Path" (Explicit Mapping)
*This tells FFmpeg exactly which stream to use, avoiding any "trailing option" confusion.*
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -map 0:v:0 -vf "crop=180:180:16:20,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an spark.webm
```

**Testing Instructions:**
1.  Copy the **entire line** for Option 1 and paste it.
2.  If it works, check the `spark.webm` file. If the background is transparent and the icon looks good, tell me **"Option 1 worked"** and I'll drop the other 5.
3.  If you get a "color" error, it means the gray background isn't `0x1a1a1a`. In that case, tell me and we will find the exact hex.

**Standing by.**

The failures were caused by the terminal breaking the lines in the wrong places or merging the `-an` flag into the codec name. 

Here are the **6 Final Alpha Strike** commands. I have formatted them as **absolute single lines**. Copy the entire block for each one and paste it into your terminal.

### ğŸ§ª THE ALPHA GHOST COMMANDS (TRUE SINGLE LINES)

**1. SPARK (Top Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:16:20,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an spark.webm
```

**2. FALCON (Top Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:248:20,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an falcon.webm
```

**3. EAGLE (Middle Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:16:249,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an eagle.webm
```

**4. OWL (Middle Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:248:249,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an owl.webm
```

**5. OWL_ALT (Bottom Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:16:478,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an owl_alt.webm
```

**6. HAWK (Bottom Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=180:180:248:478,colorkey=0x1a1a1a:0.1:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an hawk.webm
```

---

### ğŸ’¡ Troubleshooting the "Ghost" Effect:
*   **If you see a black box:** That means the background color wasn't exactly `0x1a1a1a`.

I hear youâ€”clipping on the right means the crop box is too narrow or shifted too far left for those specific cells. And the "shadow" box means the transparency key (`colorkey`) missed the mark.

To fix the **clipping**, I'm widening the frame to **220px**. 
To fix the **transparency**, I'm switching to a **High-Tolerance Black Key** (`0x000000:0.3`). If your background is a dark shadow, this will "eat" the dark pixels and leave only the glowing icon.

### ğŸ§ª THE ALPHA GHOST REPAIR (COPY & PASTE)

**1. SPARK (Top Left) - Widened**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=220:200:5:15,colorkey=0x000000:0.3:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an spark.webm
```

**2. FALCON (Top Right) - Widened**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=220:200:237:15,colorkey=0x000000:0.3:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an falcon.webm
```

**3. EAGLE (Middle Left) - Widened & Shifted**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=220:200:10:244,colorkey=0x000000:0.3:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an eagle.webm
```

**4. OWL (Middle Right) - Widened & Shifted**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=220:200:242:244,colorkey=0x000000:0.3:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an owl.webm
```

**5. OWL_ALT (Bottom Left)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=220:200:10:473,colorkey=0x000000:0.3:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an owl_alt.webm
```

**6. HAWK (Bottom Right)**
```bash
ffmpeg -i input.mp4 -vf "crop=220:200:242:473,colorkey=0x000000:0.3:0.1,format=yuva420p,scale=350:350" -c:v libvpx-vp9 -an hawk.webm
```

**YES.** It makes absolute sense. You are describing a **Context-Aware Focus HUD.** 

This layout moves away from a static dashboard and into a **Layered Command Center** where the UI physically reacts to your focus. It prioritizes the "Middle Pane" as the sacred workspace and treats the Rails as "Flyout Toolkits."

### The "Deep Dive" Layout Breakdown:

**1. The Middle Pane (The Arena):**
*   **Top Sub-Pane (The Schematic):** A persistent, high-level "Mini-Map." It stays small and clean, showing the color-coded laser flow (Yellow â” Blue â” Purple â” Green) so you always know where you are in the project's life cycle.
*   **Bottom Sub-Pane (The Pods):** 5 Industrial Cards. 
    *   **Idle:** They look like high-tech "Slots" in a rack. 
    *   **Active:** You click one (e.g., `FALCON`), and it "Mechanical Slides" open, expanding to show the deep details while simultaneously triggering the Right Rail.

**2. The Left Rail (The Arsenal/Archive):**
*   **The "Stealth" Mode:** It stays collapsed (maybe just a thin 40px sliver or completely hidden). 
*   **The Overlay:** When you expand it to pick a `START` file or a `SESSION`, it slides **over** the middle pane like a translucent glass door. 
*   **The Handshake:** You pick a session â” the data loads into the pods **behind the rail** â” you click the middle pane (The "Arena") â” the rail slams shut (collapses). This is pure focus-management.

**3. The Right Rail (The Inspection Deck):**
*   This becomes the "Active Intel" pane. It only expands when you are actually working on a phase. If you're just looking at the mind map, it stays out of the way.

**4. Visual Physics (The "Ritual"):**
*   **Mechanical Layers:** The UI shouldn't feel like a website; it should feel like layers of hardware sliding over each other. 
*   **Transparency:** Using `backdrop-filter: blur(10px)` on the expanded Left Rail so you can see the pods populating with data behind it.

### Why this works:
It solves the "Screen Crowding" problem. By letting the Left Rail overlay the workspace and then "getting out of the way" with a single click, you maximize the real estate for the 350px animated icons and the data views.

**Does this "Layered/Overlay" focus logic match the way you want to move through a session?** (Standing by, NO CODE).
